        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer649477248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9454446822930172819">Will West has always lived his life under the radar - moving every 18 months, never making friends, always striving to be average and unforgettable, just as his parents have always wanted him to be, until one morning when he sees a mysterious black sedan. "They are looking for an address they can't find," he knows. When the vehicle suddenly stops in front of him, he instantaneously receives a text from his father (who is in another city at a conference) - "RUN!" That's just what he does, out run</span>
  <span id="freeText9454446822930172819" style="display:none">Will West has always lived his life under the radar - moving every 18 months, never making friends, always striving to be average and unforgettable, just as his parents have always wanted him to be, until one morning when he sees a mysterious black sedan. "They are looking for an address they can't find," he knows. When the vehicle suddenly stops in front of him, he instantaneously receives a text from his father (who is in another city at a conference) - "RUN!" That's just what he does, out running these strangers. His day only gets stranger when he learns, The Center for Integrated Learning, an exclusive prep school is giving him a full-ride scholarship, based upon an unusually high test score. Not knowing who to trust or where to turn, armed with his fathers rules, with strangers trying to kidnap him, and his parents acting abnormal, he runs to the school, where he finds he isn't alone in his abilities and talents. Now he must find who is after him, what they have done with his parents, and where he fits in with his new-found friends. <br /><br />A bit of a Percy Jackson feel, "The Paladin Prophecy" is an action-packed, non-stop, hard-to-put-down story that lovers of Percy, Harry Potter, and John Smith (Number Four) will enjoy. Having said that, I have to admit that I am a 41-year-old mom, and I loved it too. The characters were familiar, but had enough of their own story and adventure that they were interesting and well-developed. The plot was full of action, adventure, and drama that never stopped until the last page. The ending wrapped things up nicely, yet left enough of a mystery to make me anticipate the next in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9454446822930172819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer464210774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8816088030715427296">Diving right in, the Paladin Prophecy is very fast-paced. It really reminded me of the Percy Jackson series, if you weren't told Percy had anything special about him, or why he might be doing anything he's doing.<br/><br/>The plot seems based more on action than plot, until about 2/3 of the way through the book. Frost obviously adheres to the "show, don't tell" theory in writing, which is both fun and frustrating. You don't find out why the antagonist is even after him until the final pages of the book. T</span>
  <span id="freeText8816088030715427296" style="display:none">Diving right in, the Paladin Prophecy is very fast-paced. It really reminded me of the Percy Jackson series, if you weren't told Percy had anything special about him, or why he might be doing anything he's doing.<br /><br />The plot seems based more on action than plot, until about 2/3 of the way through the book. Frost obviously adheres to the "show, don't tell" theory in writing, which is both fun and frustrating. You don't find out why the antagonist is even after him until the final pages of the book. The action feels purposeless in several scenes. There are loose ends that are never tied up, details that seem to get swept under the rug and forgotten about, and questions both major and minor that go unanswered. Here's hoping that's for the purpose of fleshing out the next book, and the juicy bits of the plot don't fall between the cracks.<br /><br />Another annoyance is the character of Dave. He seems to be the author's "get out of jail free" card, as Will never seems fully capable of fighting his own battles. In several scenes, the action takes Will and his comrades into a dead-end, plot-wise. How will the protagonist get himself out of this bind?! the reader wonders. Well, he doesn't. Ba da! Dave to the rescue. Again.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, it was a fun, easy read, and I do look forward to the second book; primarily because I have some major questions I'm looking forward to seeing answered. The author is excellent at hooking the reader into this world he's created, despite the holes in the plot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8816088030715427296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText22937154579854826" style="display:none">This is a fast paced fun read. Once I started this book I couldn't put it down. <div id="review_2085751793" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2085751793" />
    <a title="Ilse de Boer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48595697-ilse-de-boer"><img alt="Ilse de Boer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509900156p2/48595697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2085751793?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ilse de Boer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ilse de Boer" href="/user/show/48595697-ilse-de-boer">Ilse de Boer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789045206080" href="/book/show/25798343-de-paladijnse-voorspelling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48595697-ilse-de-boer?shelf=heb-ik-thuis">heb-ik-thuis</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085751793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17787968926737825050">Overall this was quite a fun book to read, but unfortunately there are some things stated in this book that I feel like I should correct.<br/>Little spoiler alert: the main person, Will, has superhuman speed. Later on, some doctors explain how it is possible that he runs so fast, but they are very, very wrong. <br/>First of all, one of the doctors says his hematocrit level is almost 100 percent. Someone with such a high hematocrit level isn't fast. He's dead. The hematocrit level shows the percentage of t</span>
  <span id="freeText17787968926737825050" style="display:none">Overall this was quite a fun book to read, but unfortunately there are some things stated in this book that I feel like I should correct.<br />Little spoiler alert: the main person, Will, has superhuman speed. Later on, some doctors explain how it is possible that he runs so fast, but they are very, very wrong. <br />First of all, one of the doctors says his hematocrit level is almost 100 percent. Someone with such a high hematocrit level isn't fast. He's dead. The hematocrit level shows the percentage of the blood that exists of red blood cells. The hematocrit of healthy people varies from approximately 36 to 51 percent. A higher hematocrit level changes the blood's structure: instead of a nice, kind of watery substance, into a more and more syrupy goo. The problem with this is that your heart can't handle that sticky stuff. To get enough oxygen to all your tissues, it has to pump harder and harder as the viscosity goes up. And unfortunately hearts can't handle that kind of stress. If stuff gets too heavy, it'll just stop beating. And yeah, that usually results in death.<br />The whole structure of blood is actually perfect. The limiting factor for excercising is not the blood, but the heart. That means that you can change whatever you want about the blood, but you will not get faster. <br />The doctors also use some other fancy words, like the corpus callosum and the prefrontal cortex, but my advise about anything medical in this book is: ignore it. Don't try to understand it. The words used are all real things, like the corpus callosum, but that's all there is to say about it. Just assume that whatever is stated is not correct. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17787968926737825050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_369139239" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/369139239" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8769426-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430689841p2/8769426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/369139239?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/8769426-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375980015" href="/book/show/13573307-the-paladin-prophecy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=e-arc">e-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=physical-arc">physical-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer369139239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9913805761745877018"><b><a href='http://booknook.me' rel='nofollow noopener'>booknook</a> — Young Adult book reviews</b><br/><br/>Oh my god. Full stop.<br/><br/><strong>This book totally awed me.</strong> I almost passed up the opportunity to read The Paladin Prophecy. It wasn't grabbing me. But on a whim, I figured <i>"Why not"</i> and got it through Netgalley. <strong>I'm so glad I did!</strong> For me, this book was right on par with <a href='http://booknook.me/insignia-by-s-j-kincaid/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Insignia</a>, both in style/story and in how much I loved it. And if you read my review of Insignia, you'll know how much I adored it and realize exactly what that statement means. <strong>It means that The Paladin Pr</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText9913805761745877018" style="display:none"><b><a href="http://booknook.me" rel="nofollow noopener">booknook</a> — Young Adult book reviews</b><br /><br />Oh my god. Full stop.<br /><br /><strong>This book totally awed me.</strong> I almost passed up the opportunity to read The Paladin Prophecy. It wasn't grabbing me. But on a whim, I figured <i>"Why not"</i> and got it through Netgalley. <strong>I'm so glad I did!</strong> For me, this book was right on par with <a href="http://booknook.me/insignia-by-s-j-kincaid/" rel="nofollow noopener">Insignia</a>, both in style/story and in how much I loved it. And if you read my review of Insignia, you'll know how much I adored it and realize exactly what that statement means. <strong>It means that The Paladin Prophecy is insanely "knock-your-pants-off and leave you butt naked but you won't even care because you're too busy reading" awesome.</strong> It's like Harry Potter style school/fantasy, meets "kids save the world" Percy Jackson, meets insanely awesome mind-blowing "OHMYGOD I WANT THAT" technology, meets the page-turning awe that is Dan Brown conspiracy/history-brought-to-life/secret society. Put it all together and you get this incredibly original story that will suck you in and won't let you go.<br /><br /><strong>The first thing I have to talk about is the characters, because holy crap, the characters are really what make this book absolutely freakin' incredible.</strong> Every single character in this book is so alive and filled with amazing personality. I actually didn't fully appreciate Will's character until maybe 100+ pages into the book. The first part of the book is largely Will on his own, running from danger, and maybe interacting with one or two people here and there. <strong>But when Will settles into his new group of friends, he really comes alive!</strong> He has this cocky, witty personality that really shines when he's stepping up to bullies. He doesn't take any crap from them and he makes that so obvious. IT'S AWESOME!!! Like, wow.<br /><br />The other characters in the book are equally amazing. They're all hilarious and quirky in their own ways and had me cracking up. I want to be friends with these people! Seriously! Where can I find them?? Why aren't my friends that cool??<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I happen to be sitting on the sickest, most awesome idea for a social network site ever. [...] I take all the best parts of YouTube, Twitter, and Facebook, and combine them into a whole new service called... YouTwit-face."</i>
  <br />
  <br />
  <cite>—ARC of The Paladin Prophecy, Page 173</cite>
</blockquote><br /><br />As for the story, sometimes I honestly felt like I had no idea what the heck was going on, but I didn't care, because something kept me absolutely glued to this book. <strong>I just sat down and read and read and read, because I had to know what the heck was going on and I was eager to absorb every word until my eyes bled!</strong> I literally had no idea where this book was leading for the longest time. <strong>I just couldn't get my head around what to expect — is this magic? Is this kick-ass X-Men genetic evolution? Is this Dan Brown conspiracy? I had no idea, but it just wasn't something I was worrying about.</strong> I was too busy cracking up over the hilarious dialogue, or wishing the characters existed in real life, or just enjoying the action and mysterious plot as it was developing. I realized that this book is about the ride; it's about the not knowing; and it's about trying to solve the mystery of what's going on.<br /><br />Throughout the book, we learn about 100 different "rules to live by" that Will's father drilled into him as he was growing up. At first I thought these rules were kind of weird and cheesy but pretty soon I was retracting that statement. They're pretty awesome, and surprisingly good advice. They definitely gave the story a little something extra, since they kept popping up in good moments. <strong>I actually felt like I was learning life advice from this book, as weird as that sounds!</strong> here are a few examples:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>#5 TRUST NO ONE<br />#7 DON'T CONFUSE GOOD LUCK WITH A GOOD PLAN<br />#26 ONCE IS AN ANOMALY. TWICE IS A COINCIDENCE. THREE TIMES IS A PATTERN. AND AS WE KNOW... <br />#27 SOMETIMES THE ONLY WAY TO DEAL WITH A BULLY IS TO HIT FIRST. HARD.</i>
  <br />
  <br />
  <cite>—ARC of The Paladin Prophecy</cite>
</blockquote><br /><br />I won't reveal anymore because part of the fun of the book is seeing these rules for yourself as the story develops. ;)<br /><br />The end of this book was an absolute whirlwind of action and puzzles. Parts of it were honestly a little confusing to me, but I think that might have been the formatting on my e-ARC. We suddenly hear from a bunch of different points of view but there were no section separators (and not even extra line breaks) to tell me when the POV was switching, so it got a little crazy. But I'm sure this will probably be better laid out in the final copies!<br /><br />I definitely recommend this book a hundred times over if you like action, mystery, a bit of science, and some crazy fantasy X-Men type stuff. <strong>This book could easily be the next Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympians!</strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="9913805761745877018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer711055834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14708238009505254891"><b>Buddy read with </b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4159427-athena' rel='nofollow noopener'>Athena</a><br/><br/><b>Actual rating: 4.5 stars. Any spoilers will be clearly marked. </b><br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/Happy' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381415036ra/4833509.gif' alt='Happy photo: happy happy.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>That was such a stinking fun book!!!! It's also quite different from most books I've read. It was totally not what I was expecting to walk into when I picked it up. But that was ok and it worked for me. <br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/Hug' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393743791ra/8758474.gif' alt='Hug photo: hug hug.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I developed such a bond and liking for the characters, which is also something I totally didn't see coming. My heart ached for Will, and he ended up breaking me just a little. I loved Nick and Ajay endles</span>
  <span id="freeText14708238009505254891" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with </b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4159427-athena" rel="nofollow noopener">Athena</a><br><br><b>Actual rating: 4.5 stars. Any spoilers will be clearly marked. </b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/Happy" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381415036ra/4833509.gif" alt="Happy photo: happy happy.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>That was such a stinking fun book!!!! It's also quite different from most books I've read. It was totally not what I was expecting to walk into when I picked it up. But that was ok and it worked for me. <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/Hug" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393743791ra/8758474.gif" alt="Hug photo: hug hug.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I developed such a bond and liking for the characters, which is also something I totally didn't see coming. My heart ached for Will, and he ended up breaking me just a little. I loved Nick and Ajay endlessly!!! Nick felt so down to earth and real to me. I even ended up developing a soft spot for Elise and Brooke, whom I didn't totally care for in the beginning. <br><br>Will is sort of thrust into a nightmare from page one. There was lots of action right from the opening page. Absolutely <b>zero</b> dull moments. We follow him to a school for extraordinarily smart kids. It just so happens Will ends up with kids that also possess extraordinary skills. What transpires is something out of this world, seriously. Will is a special person with all sorts of spectacular abilities. <s>I'm beyond envious of his running ability.</s> The ending is left open, which is to be expected since it's the first in a series. This is a series I will definitely be continuing. <br><br>There were a couple of issues, quite minor, that I had with the story. I felt like some things just happened too easily, and ended up feeling a little predictable. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It just seemed too convenient that Will wakes up and finds he's being watched/followed, goes to school and is pulled into the principal's office to be informed he kicked ass on the score of that test, and magically there's someone there offering him this trip to this school fully paid for. Then poof! He's in desperate need of somewhere to run and hide to. I kept waiting for it to be the school behind all of it. I dunno...it just felt off. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The issues I had were quite small, but did earn a half star deduction. All in all, it's a totally fun book with a different set of things happening. I had fun!! <br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14708238009505254891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

He's moved countless times and his abides by rules that his father set forth and lives off of them like its his bible. Will was a character that I liked, he was smart (obviously), funny, but quite pompous and reminded me of a young and modern Sherlock Holmes in a way. But Will was the only thing about the book that I could really watch a</span>
  <span id="freeText8174171300803590090" style="display:none"><b>More reviews at <a href="http://rondoofpossibleworld.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Rondo of a Possible World: YA Book Reviews </a> </b><br /><br />Will West is a genius told to dumb it down and remain low because there is danger lurking after him. He's moved countless times and his abides by rules that his father set forth and lives off of them like its his bible. Will was a character that I liked, he was smart (obviously), funny, but quite pompous and reminded me of a young and modern Sherlock Holmes in a way. But Will was the only thing about the book that I could really watch and connect with while the entirety of the situation he was in and the background details left me confused.<br /><br />While I wanted to keep reading for Will's sake and for his adoring persona and wanting to find out what the "Paladin Prophecy", the reason why the title got it's name, was or the reason why Will was in danger from the get-go, I was just bored with what was going on and I couldn't connect with the book, making me confused and glide through the pages forgetting what I had just previously read. Also, the intake of characters left me dazed and overwhelmed.<br /><br /><i><b>Final Summation:</b> While this wasn't the book for me, I have read countless reviews that raved over the book. I'm sure others will think so too, but</i> The Paladin Prophecy <i> just wasn't enough to keep me entertained and heal my confusion, leaving me to put the book down.</i></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer790392457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6631203917072519800">How wonderful to read a Young Adult fantasy that doesn't have a steamy love triangle in it! What it does have is a strong action filled plot, characters that behave like teenagers, or at least teenagers with superpowers, and a mystery surrounding the source of the superpowers and the origins of the evil opposition. This book is long, but I found myself finishing it in just a few days because it was hard to put down. The basic premise is a boarding school that is targeted toward gifted teens, and</span>
  <span id="freeText6631203917072519800" style="display:none">How wonderful to read a Young Adult fantasy that doesn't have a steamy love triangle in it! What it does have is a strong action filled plot, characters that behave like teenagers, or at least teenagers with superpowers, and a mystery surrounding the source of the superpowers and the origins of the evil opposition. This book is long, but I found myself finishing it in just a few days because it was hard to put down. The basic premise is a boarding school that is targeted toward gifted teens, and we're not talking about kids who are good in math. The gifts seem like extraordinary powers, but not as extreme as the X-Men. The school also has some evil opposition that have their own set up special abilities. The first half of the book was a 5 star read for me. I felt the ending was a bit rushed, but I am still on board for reading the sequel.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15684332706294371080">Minor quibble with the fact that Brooke basically had no personality or purpose other than to be a damsel in distress at the right moment, but I am hoping she will get more fully fleshed out in the sequels. Also, the first couple of chapters were super confusing - I think the idea is that you, along with Will, are supposed to suddenly be thrust into the action with no idea why things are happening, and I think that makes sense for a screenplay but can make for a rough start to a novel. Overall t</span>
  <span id="freeText15684332706294371080" style="display:none">Minor quibble with the fact that Brooke basically had no personality or purpose other than to be a damsel in distress at the right moment, but I am hoping she will get more fully fleshed out in the sequels. Also, the first couple of chapters were super confusing - I think the idea is that you, along with Will, are supposed to suddenly be thrust into the action with no idea why things are happening, and I think that makes sense for a screenplay but can make for a rough start to a novel. Overall though, it was a fun and entertaining read with likeable characters, a good central mystery, and some unique world building. I will most likely read the sequels at some point.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2104608923" />
    <a title="Olivia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2701062-olivia"><img alt="Olivia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526931411p2/2701062.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2104608923?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivia" href="/user/show/2701062-olivia">Olivia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375871061" href="/book/show/14823574-the-paladin-prophecy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2701062-olivia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2701062-olivia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2701062-olivia?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2701062-olivia?shelf=read-for-school">read-for-school</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2104608923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8258957164093758093">Maybe good for reluctant readers with its fast pace, but more avid readers might find it harder to overlook the familiar beats and tropes and clunky writing. Also, all teens are going to find these kids to talk exactly like an adult imagines teens do, which is a laughable effort.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_300756168" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300756168" />
    <a title="Jody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4233749-jody"><img alt="Jody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310070875p2/4233749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300756168?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody" href="/user/show/4233749-jody">Jody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Library Binding 9780375970450" href="/book/show/13414545-the-paladin-prophecy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4233749-jody?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4233749-jody?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4233749-jody?shelf=special-abilities">special-abilities</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300756168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11516222425397821155">The Paladin Prophecy is a full on action movie where "Bourne Identity" meets Harry Potter. I was immediately drawn into the action where Will West hits the ground running literally from mysterious black sedans. Will has always lived by a book of rules his Dad made for him. Will never preformed up to his abilities and always stayed below the radar. He wasn't even able to join the cross-country team until he promised to always finish in the pack. But as the book starts, Will notices the black seda</span>
  <span id="freeText11516222425397821155" style="display:none">The Paladin Prophecy is a full on action movie where "Bourne Identity" meets Harry Potter. I was immediately drawn into the action where Will West hits the ground running literally from mysterious black sedans. Will has always lived by a book of rules his Dad made for him. Will never preformed up to his abilities and always stayed below the radar. He wasn't even able to join the cross-country team until he promised to always finish in the pack. But as the book starts, Will notices the black sedans watching and following his running route. After escaping to school, Will is called out of class to be offered a full scholarship to THE CENTER, an ultra exclusive school for the highest of achievers. Will finds out that he scored off the charts of a regular exam he took in the fall. Will figures his parents will be angry due to a violation of the rule to never draw attention to himself. But when he gets home, he finds his Mom has been replaced by Stepford Mom, his mother by looks but who is not acting like herself at all and won't take her sunglasses off. Will decides to run away and almost gets caught by some really demonstrous bad guys. He is saved by a guardian of sorts who will not tell him what is going on.<br /><br />Will struggles to escape the black caps who have captured his Dad and done something to his Mom. Desperate to get away, he calls Dr. Robbins and accepts the scholarship to the center. He barely escapes to the center when he is immediately challenged by a fellow student who is essentially the dorm advisor and security. Will finds himself immediately thrust into a world of over-achievers that are mysterious and trustworthy. Will finds a "family" of sorts that he learns to trust and even violates rules. Will belongs with the center but knows that he hasn't really escaped the danger that found him in the Southern California hills. Soon Will finds a connection that challenges everything he has ever known. Will must piece together a mystery that could mean keeping the balance between light and dark. With the help of his friends, Will uncovers the secrets that have been hidden in the world since before the English ever landed in America.<br /><br />I loved this book and cannot wait for the next one. This is the start of solid series in the fashion of Harry Potter. I could totally see this playing out as a movie in the genre of Percy Jackson or HP. The story hits the ground running and continues to engage the reader in a mysterious identity of Will. Will West is also the best hero name in a long time! I do wish there was a little more romance between Will and Brooke--It seemed rushed and an afterthought in the whole picture. It didn't really need to be there but being the hopeless romantic I am I hope this will develop more in the future books. The struggle of light and dark reminded me of the darkness that was written into Scott Westerfields' Midnight Hour books. I would recommend this book to anyone who enjoys action filled struggle between good and evil. This series is poised to burst onto the YA scene and become the next breakout.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11516222425397821155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1238481181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1238481181" />
    <a title="gabi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40447521-gabi"><img alt="gabi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597861508p2/40447521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1238481181?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="gabi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="gabi" href="/user/show/40447521-gabi">gabi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375980015" href="/book/show/13573307-the-paladin-prophecy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1238481181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7978769254022419987">I read this for the first time over a year ago. Recently I decided to do a random reread. It was just as good as the first time, if not better. This time though I will continue with the series.<br/><br/>Will West has lived his whole life pretending to be normal, getting average grades, and moving about every fifteen months. His parents have never given him any real explanation, but he trusts them. Then he makes a mistake and scores extraordinary high on a nationwide exam. Now people want him to go to an e</span>
  <span id="freeText7978769254022419987" style="display:none">I read this for the first time over a year ago. Recently I decided to do a random reread. It was just as good as the first time, if not better. This time though I will continue with the series.<br /><br />Will West has lived his whole life pretending to be normal, getting average grades, and moving about every fifteen months. His parents have never given him any real explanation, but he trusts them. Then he makes a mistake and scores extraordinary high on a nationwide exam. Now people want him to go to an exclusive prep school and he’s followed by black sedans. Then when something strange happens to his mom, he runs. His skills are put to the test and he realizes the rules that his parents taught him to live by may just save his life.<br /><br />The characters were really good. Will had unknowingly been prepared for this (Whatever “this” is.). He is really smart and quiet, but not shy. He never let’s down his guard. Sine he’s been taught to not trust anyone, he hides his true self from everyone. Ajay is funny (usually when he isn’t meaning to be). He’s Southern with the accent that goes along with it (which I love). Of all of them, he probably gets scared the easiest. He has some great skills and is like a genius with technology. Nick is a gymnast. He’s hilarious and is rarely ever serious, but fiercely loyal to his friends. He’s not so very smart, but he knows his sports. Elise is like an Eygptian queen, literally. When she looks at you, it feels like she is reading your thoughts. She is a beautiful piano player and singer. Brooke is the parent over them all. She’s cautious, but brave. She’s kind and caring.<br /><br />This book was exciting from the start. Even when reading it a second time I flew through it. It was very fast paced. The running, the car chases, and then the new school was all intense. There was so many questions and intrigue. Especially concerning Will himself, his abilities were really neat. The monsters and who knows what else that were after Will were weird and ugly, but interesting. I need more answers. Everything must be figured out soon! The ending was intense and I was on the edge of my seat. That kidnapping! Those fighting scenes! They were great.<br /><br />There was a kiss or two, but nothing major. There was language, not a lot, but not a little either. Words like d***, d***, b****** were common. F*** was in the book once or twice, but only the letter “f” was shown. God’s name was used in vain quite a few times.<br /><br />Overall, this was a good book. I’m excited to see how this turns out. I recommend this to a little older teens (or just more mature teens) for some of the language, but was very neat.<br /><br />You can check out this review on my blog too, at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://aheartredeemed.wordpress.com/2016/06/15/book-review-the-paladin-prophecy-the-paladin-prophecy-book-1/">https://aheartredeemed.wordpress.com/...</a> Thanks!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7978769254022419987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_427948371" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/427948371" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2446219-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319409884p2/2446219.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/427948371?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/2446219-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Library Binding 9780375970450" href="/book/show/13414545-the-paladin-prophecy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer427948371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer392322777111052431">One day my boyfriend and I randomly stumbled into a horror book/dvd/gift shop. There happened to be a book signing that day by Mark Frost, for his new book The Paladin Prophecy. I didn't pay too much attention to it (sadly there was only one person there for the signing) but as I was browsing I overheard that Mark Frost was the co-creator of Twin Peaks. I love Twin Peaks, and I have a friend who LOVES Twin Peaks and all of a sudden I really wanted this guy's autograph. I picked up his book and w</span>
  <span id="freeText392322777111052431" style="display:none">One day my boyfriend and I randomly stumbled into a horror book/dvd/gift shop. There happened to be a book signing that day by Mark Frost, for his new book The Paladin Prophecy. I didn't pay too much attention to it (sadly there was only one person there for the signing) but as I was browsing I overheard that Mark Frost was the co-creator of Twin Peaks. I love Twin Peaks, and I have a friend who LOVES Twin Peaks and all of a sudden I really wanted this guy's autograph. I picked up his book and was a little surprised to find it was a mystery/supernatural Young Adult novel. I like mystery/supernatural YA so I bought the book and got his autograph (actually I made my boyfriend get his autograph but they soon figured out the ploy and it was super embarrassing, but anyway...) <br /><br />Unfortunately the book was pretty bad. It's about a boy with a mysterious past. His parents have moved him around his entire life, and always told him not to draw attention to himself, and to suppress his talents. Then all of a sudden men in black hats and creepy monsters from another dimension start chasing him and take over his parents. He is forced to flee to a school for the gifted, but he's not safe even there. The school is part of a huge conspiracy somehow linking these monsters with the school's secret society. But luckily he makes friends with his misfit roommates, all of whom have secret powers of their own.<br /><br />Okay, first off I'm not a fan of weird gross bug-monsters. They just feel kind of silly and dumb. Then he throws in something about guardian angels that work at a huge company in the sky. Add that to the fact that the writing just wasn't that good. Then mix in some ridiculous "teen slang" that sounds like what an 80 year old man think kids sound like. Have you ever heard a current teenager say "Dorkus Malorkus"? What about "Chillax, Slackasaurus"? It's like the comic relief was so forced it made the whole story ridiculous.<br /><br />I was pretty disappointed to get this type of writing from someone who was involved in such a pivotal TV show. The book did start to improve towards the end when the whole conspiracy was revealed about why the kids have these powers. I'm totally on board with that story line (**cough, cough, also it's a lot like the YA novel I'm currently writing, cough cough**)I just wish these weird demon monsters weren't a part of it. I think the second book might be more interesting, although I'm not sure if I can make it through much more of these kids slang.</span>
  <a data-text-id="392322777111052431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6IHqQG9mh7tu6NfknRIUXR1WEQpuZd+57/CsrWxI251V7ejXgq9cy9Ofu6PDoiduURY14nRS6p+fWGOLIT6B+Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dTmqLFxP3uJduQBA0RTI9qCSMs3p0HN6CmvdIWb0SUnIVai7sYYFkuDObAePpPvF7NIWJfPnRlx6wxIHK4ITLQ==')})
  }
